<date>1574196285204<//date><Rate>5< /Rate><review>My very first visit was for a Botox update on forehead, eyes and bunny lines. I absolutely loved Shawnda. She explained the procedure and discussed all of the expectations for during and post procedure. It did not hurt at all and I had no bruising which is usually never the case for me.

I later decided to have my tear troughs filled. I have had the procedure done twice before - first time with a VERY famous Beverly Hills doctor that is known for his lip work on a VERY famous cosmetics company owner who is known specifically for her lips. The last time I had this done I had to return for several follow up visits because if you don't know your eye area is very thin and deciding to have this procedure I hope you will do your homework and not expect a one visit miracle. Due to the fact that you are working in such a delicate area, it may take several visits to get the balance you need between eyes and cheek. Luckily, I only required the one visit. I was impressed once again that I had almost no bruising and loved my results with just the first visit.

Next up, I signed up for the Hydra facials. Love love love love love. Do yourself a favor and just get it done as a treat to yourself. You can never have enough hydration living in San Diego! My Esthetician for the facials was an absolute pleasure to visit with and also was so in depth about the procedure and expectations. I will be doing this again and again.

Most recently, I am having the Diamond Polar treatment on my neck for sagging jowls and what looks like a gobble gobble, loose skin. I hate it. I signed up for ten sessions and currently half way through my treatment. I absolutely love the way the treatment feels on my skin each week. It is so relaxing and to be honest...I would pay just to go spend that time with Marissa. If you have not met her yet  - you are truly missing out. She is beyond precious and THE MOST CARING EVER. Love love love her! I really can't post just yet about my final results but I will once I am done. I have already noticed some firming up but I also feel like I am a realist in knowing I still might need some Kybella also.

I would like to just give a great big shout out to Linda who has patiently put up with me having to reschedule and schedule last minute appointments. She is always such a sweetheart on the phone and via emails. I so appreciate that I can just email, text or call and boom they are always responsive to get me in as soon as possible when I have a need.

I want to urge all of you out there to please understand just how lucky you are to have such a talented, caring team here in San Marcos/North County. I have had soooo many cosmetic surgeries and procedures in the past - all over the country. I could do just about anywhere and willing to pay any price (and have) but I love the way these girls make me feel. I know them, I know there struggles and how absolutely hard they work. I have followed them on social media since my very first visit. They are real people and even in San Marcos, they make me feel like I am back in my small town Texas!

Through out my year as a client, I have witnessed all to often others taking extreme advantage of these sweet girls. From flat out theft, to scamming services and not paying and then the overall customers no showing appointments. My mom was a hairdresser growing up so I know the importance of schedules and not being a jerk to others. Everyone of these girls have families...I beg you...please keep your appointments with them! They are busy and they make a choice to take time to help make us all feel better about our looks. The least we can do is be KIND and THOUGHTFUL when booking their time.

Lastly, Shawnda is very talented and I absolutely trust her completely at this point. She is very professional and works so hard to make sure her clients are completely satisfied. Again, I have treated all over the US with full fledged cosmetic surgeons. Be thankful you have these girls locally!<//review>< Pictures>

<Date>1527477548181< /Date>< username>
Amado Carino</username>
< review>
Kind of hole-in-the-wall place for Peruvian fare in Lake Forest, not some fancy diner for trendy people. It's the kind of place where people go to savor food that they grew up with, prepared in as close a possible to grandma's cooking. The paella is prepared differently compared to the Spanish or Mexican version, garnished with a different set of herbs. The chicken grilled with the flatiron is something to behold, so tender on the inside and crispy on the outside. If you are adventurous, they offer grilled cow heart for your taking. Parking is free. Accepts all major credit cards except American Express.<//review>

< username>
Felix Lee<//username>
< date>
1450815874755<//date>
<Rate>4<//Rate><Review>Delicias Peruanas is a family-operated Peruvian restaurant in Lake Forest. The family is Japanese-Peruvian, with father in the kitchen, mother behind the counter, and son as the sever. Japanese and Peruvian may sound like an unusual combination, but Japanese-Peruvians represent 0.3% of the population in Peru. During the Sino-Japanese War in the late 1800's, the economy of Japan suffered and it produced a surplus of local farmers. Peru welcomed the immigration of hard working Japanese farmers. These Japanese immigrants combined their native recipes with Peru's favorable fishing environment and the rice imported by the Spanish, giving rise to unique Japanese-inspired-Peruvian dishes prepared with novel cooking styles (Nikkei cuisine).

Although the chef and son at Delicias Peruanas have Japanese blood and possess an Asian appearance, they speak fluent Spanish. The chef cooks authentic Peruvian dishes (with Asian flair) and the server Roberto is competent in describing the differences in each dish.

During lunch, a $8 special is available, which is affordable given that it consists of a selection among 4 Peruvian-inspired entrees with generous portion, a soup/salad, a citrus concentrate beverage, and bread with aji sauce. For a light eater, this can be equivalent to two meals.

The soup was similar to a garden vegetable soup but also resembled a clear version of an Italian minestrone. Zucchini, celery, cabbage, lima beans, and cilantro were found. The bread was standard but the spicy aji sauce was remarkable. The citrus beverage was a refreshing juice with passion fruit flavors, appropriate for the summertime.

The main course that I ordered was the estofado de pollo. Two pieces of tender chicken (thigh and leg) were garnished with pepper, herbs, and mild spices. The chicken was placed in a thin tomato sauce and served over a bed of rice, two pieces of potato, and sliced red onions. I recommend this dish to those who prefer wet food since estofado de pollo is a chicken stew over rice. For those who prefer dry food, I recommend the pescado frito (pan fried tilapia) dish available on the lunch special menu. The dishes are not fully representative of traditional Peruvian cuisine, it's fits the Peruvian-American fusion tastes.

While I waited for my lunch, I observed the kitchen and discovered that the chef cooking with an open fire and a flambe technique. I don't think every dish is prepared this way, but it was quite a sight to see the chef hold a small pan engulfed with 3' high flames!

Delicias Peruanas is no longer a hidden hole in the wall. Word has gotten out about this gem in Lake Forest, so don't be surprised to encounter a lunch crowd. I am eager to return soon and try the other $8 lunch specials.</Review>< pictures>
None</pictures>

<Date>1558935026899</Date><Rate>5< /Rate><Text>I purchased my mattress from Mattress Firm a little over a year ago (original review below) and I wanted to upgrade my pillows. I initial bought some cheap pillows off of Amazon when I purchased my bed and now a year later and the pillows are lumpy and causing me some discomfort in my neck. I decided it was time to invest in some good quality pillows, so I reached out to Mesfin who was still with the company (thank God!) and he advised me that I should come into the store during their Memorial Day Sale to test out some options.

Mesfin educated me on the importance of a good pillow. He had me test out several pillows, on the exact make and model of the bed that I initial purchased from Mattress Firm, so that I could see how the pillow felt on top of my actual bed! I purchased 2 great pillows. I'm so glad that I did not purchase the pillows online and that I took the time to come into the store. I am even more thankful that Mesfin helped me with something so trival as picking out pillows.

Once again, I've had a great experience with Mattress Firm & Mesfin. I will be going back for all my future mattress and of course pillow needs!

Review as of 2/22/18

As a woman I am always leery of being taken advantage of when it comes to things such as getting any work done on my vehicle, or in this case buying a brand-new mattress.  I went to Mattress Firm to do some preliminary research before I made a purchase. I was greeted by the store manager, Mesfin, who was welcoming and personable. He took me around the show room and educated me on each mattress. He was extremely knowledgeable about their selection of mattresses and was very patient with me. I tested each one out and by process of elimination, he helped me find the perfect mattress for me. He took his time and answered all my questions, he really exceeded all my expectations. When I was finally ready to make my purchase 2 weeks later, he even helped me get financing!  Overall, I had a pleasant experience, Mesfin took the nervousness and anxiety out of making such a huge purchase.</Text>< pics>

<userid>107589524474345777412</userid><Text>I give Sushi House a solid 3 stars, the sushi rolls were good, but not spectacular. The bento boxes were huge, the over all quality and quantity was definitely a good value for the price. For two people we had sushi rolls, bento boxes and soft drinks all for $77.

The menu is quite large, five pages. One page is nothing but pictures of all the sushi roll with the name listed under neeth. Great idea for anyone new to sushi.

For dinning out midweek, I was very suprized how busy it was. We didn't feel rushed, but the wait staff seemed to be overwhelmed. At one point I think I counted six sushi chef's behind the counter, but three or four wait staff to deal with well over fourty tables in the main dining area. This is most definitely a high volume establishment.

I was disappointed with the fact that they did not have any seared items, Like seared Ahi tuna. Also be prepared to take home left overs.

If you are new eating sushi or have never tried it but have wanted to Sushi House would be a good place to start.<//Text>< user_name>
Ron cooking Garlets< /user_name>

< Review>
Not the world's greatest sushi rolls, but they are HUGE. For under $40 for two, I can walk out of here absolutely stuffed (+1 for that because I usually walk out of sushi restaurants still hungry after dropping $100).

I think this place used to be a Coco's or something, and it still feels like it inside. The atmosphere is loud, a few tables look like fold-out card tables to squeeze more people in, and it almost has a cafeteria-like feel. I was expecting a food fight to break out at any time. But you do get a decent view of the water.

So go to get stuffed with mediocre sushi, but don't expect an upscale, top-notch sushi restaurant.< /Review>

0x808f86a45a3d7401:0x50ee9025dc45fa4b< /Gmap_id>
< Review>
This place is reasonably close to my office, so I go here for lunch/dinner quite often. We also had a few company outings here. This is not really authentic Japanese restaurant. One of my Korean coworkers told me the place is owned by a Korean. The food is still quite delicious though (approved by one of my visiting Japanese coworker).

My favorite is the Sake Don. It's basically slices of salmon sashimi, tamago on a bed of sushi rice. They also give slices of lemon. Very fresh, very delicious, generous serving. What more can you ask?

As for the rolls, the serve several fusion dishes like baked scallion rolls. It's definitely different, definitely can't be found in Japan, but definitely good. Bring friends so you can share different varieties of rolls, or just bring a date and enjoy a short walk in the beach afterwards (bring layers, it can get pretty cold).< /Review>

Ivan Yudhi< /username>

<username>Sam S</username>< Review>
I often go to Sushi House because it is close and affordable.  The wait for this restaurant is pretty long and it lasts late into the night.

I usually get the bimbibap salad which is a bed of salad greens tossed with chrysanthemum leaves and roughly chopped raw garlic and topped with sashimi (salmon, tuna, and tako).  They give a sweet and spicy Korean hot sauce so that people can customize the spiciness.  A bowl of rice is also provided to chow down this dish.  This is a delicious and refreshing dish although not always a hit because of the raw garlic and potential less than premium fish.

Everyone always raves about the Lion King Roll, which is pretty good, but not necessarily worth the almost $12 price tag.  The roll is a baked salmon roll with a sweet miso mayo sauce.  Tasty, but if you have tried it once, try something else on their extensive menu.

Also Sushi House is Korean owned and operated, not necessarily important, but if you are looking for authentic Japanese food this might not be that place.<//Review>

<user_name>Noelle Ham<//user_name><rating>2<//rating><response>None<//response><gmapID>0x808f86a45a3d7401:0x50ee9025dc45fa4b</gmapID>< UserId.>
116796911158844589160</UserId.>
<text>I wanted to see the hype because it seems like Sushi House is famous, even for those not that familiar to Alameda.

I ordered the 2 item bento box with salmon terriyaki and tempura (1 piece of shrimp and a few veggies). My friends ordered a lion king roll and orange blossom roll, and the other ordered the katsu donburi. The bento box and katsu donburi come with soup and salad.

The sushi came out first. The orange blossom roll wasn't bad, the salmon wrapped around tasted fresh. But overall nothing impressive. The infamous lion king roll was fine. But definitely not rolled very well. Just picking it up it fell apart.

The katsu donburi bowl came out next. I didn't try any of it but my friend seemed unenthusiastic. She was picking around it, and the katsu looked soggy.

After about 20 min my box finally came out. The tempura was cold and bit soggy. The salmon was warm. It seemed like the entire time I was waiting for my box, my food was just sitting there. Meh.

The service was poor. Our waitress seemed rude and every time we asked for anything we'd get an eye roll. We didn't get spoons when she dropped off our soups (we just drank it from the bowl because we were starving) and then when my friend asked for a spoon for her katsu bowl, she handed her a plastic spoon. Seriously? There was a waitress that was going around filling waters and also cashed us out, she seemed nice though!

Do I see the hype? NOPE! There's better sushi places to eat in Alameda.</text></record></dataset><record>
